Isolated Artifacts
A single lithic flake was recovered from test B-1 at 40 to 50 cmbs but no other cultural item was
found in this test or from other shovel tests in the immediately surrounding area. As a result, this
find was designated an isolated artifact and is not considered a cultural resource site.
A single lithic flake was recovered between 20 to 40 cmbs of test K-1 but no other cultural item
was found in this test or from other shovel tests in the immediately surrounding area. As a result,
this find was designated an isolated artifact and is not considered a cultural resource site.

Ecological Communications Corporation

Page 47

Cultural Resource Inventories of Selected Areas at Four Lakes in East Texas

4.5 WHITE OAK CREEK MITIGATION AREA
The single parcel within the WOCMA was investigated using a slightly different strategy than
the rest of the inventory. Two previously recorded sites, 41MX29 and 41MX30, were known
and the purpose of fieldwork was to delineate the limits of these sites within the boundaries of
the parcel. Locations of shovel tests are plotted in Appendix A.
4.5.1 Site 41MX29
Previously recorded site 41MX29 is located at the extreme south of the inventory parcel
immediately south of the paved road. The site is at an elevation of 255 ft AMSL and consists of
a small, low mound on the east bank of Village Creek. The mound measures about 15 to 20 m in
diameter but it is not clear whether the mound is a prehistoric feature or the result of recent
dredging. The latter possibility is suggested by the partial burial near the base of the mound of a
tree estimated to be 30-40 years old.
Six shovel tests were dug in the site location plus several more tests at further distances, between
this site and 41MX30. Of the six tests, two were dug north of the road and four were dug south
of the road. Cultural material was recovered only from the single test that was placed directly on
top of the mound itself. This test (JH-1) was dug to 90 cm with a profile of massive yellowishred sandy loam. Two lithic flakes were recovered from 40 to 60 cm. No ceramics, bone, or
ground items were recovered. Elsewhere off the mound itself, the soil profiles were highly
variable with clay at depths ranging from 0 to 60 cm (Table 4-21). Mottling was noted in several
of the tests and surface disturbances were noted east of the site. A sketch map is presented in
Figure 4-19.

Previous shovel testing of this site in 1990 yielded similar
results. Of six shovel tests dug in 1990, only the two on top of
the mound were positive and the four off the mound were all
negative. The two positive tests recovered lithic flakes and some
bone fragments. No ceramics were recovered and no artifacts
were noted on the surface or eroding from the mound. The 1990
investigation concluded that the site “seems to be associated
only with the mound. We found no evidence of its extension
beyond it” (41MX29 site form).

Together, the 1990 and 2002 investigations resulted in 12 tests. Of these, only the three tests
directly on top of the mound itself were positive; the nine tests surrounding the mound were all
negative (Table 4-22). On the basis of this distribution of artifacts, the site therefore appears to
be restricted to the mound itself. This area is 15 to 20 m in diameter. However, the limited data
returns provided by the shovel testing tactics do not allow a clear assessment of site research
value. Although the site is situated on a mound, no ceramics were recovered. The lack of artifact
diversity may be a function of sample size or it may be culturally meaningful. The site could be a
small prehistoric habitation site, or it may contain only secondary deposits resulting from recent
earth moving activities. As a result, it is unknown whether or not the site may or may not be
eligible for inclusion to the NRHP. Further investigation is warranted to resolve this issue and it

4.5.2 Site 41MX30
Previously recorded site 41MX30 is located at the extreme eastern edge of the inventory parcel
on a terrace above the east bank of Village Creek. The site is at an elevation of about 300 ft
AMSL and is situated between the paved road and Village Creek. This site was initially
recorded in 1990, when 14 shovel tests were positive of 16 that were placed in a north-south
linear pattern along the terrace. However, only one of these tests was placed west of the main
line of positive tests, and it was undetermined to what degree the site might extend beyond the
terrace onto the flood plain to the west. Dimensions of the site were estimated as 400 m north to
south by about 60 m east to west. The site was thought to be perhaps associated with 41MX29
which is located about 100 m to the southwest.
The scope of the current investigation was limited to defining the boundaries of the site along its
western edge. To this extent, a total of 40 tests were placed on the flood plain between Village
Creek and the previously established line of positive tests. These tests were placed in four
inventory transects that paralleled the terrace slope. All of these tests were placed west of the
line of positive tests on the terrace and no investigation was conducted along the eastern edge of
the site. Of these 40 tests, two nearest to Village Creek could not be dug due to standing water.
Another six tests became saturated before encountering clay. Of the 38 attempted tests, only one
was positive. This test (5) was along the easternmost of the four inventory transects and was
located within the boundaries of 41MX30 as previously delineated. This test recovered a single
silicified wood flake from 15 to 30 cm. All of the remaining 37 tests on the flood plain below
the terrace were negative, including six tests that were placed between the southwestern
boundary of the site and 41MX29.
Soils were generally shallow. Ten of the 32 tests (31%) that did not encounter standing water hit
clay within the top 10 cm and only two of the tests (5%) could be dug to 80 cm without
encountering clay (Table 4-23). On average, clay

appears to be restricted to the higher terrace landform to the east. This landform is located off of
the WOCMA fee lands.

5.0 CONCLUSIONS
5.1 SUMMARY OF RESULTS
This cultural resources inventory included parcels at five separate locations in seven counties of
East Texas. The sample was defined as consisting of 1,810 acres at 12 individual parcels.
Parcels ranged in size from 11 acres to 438 acres and averaged 151 acres in size.
Field methods included pedestrian inventory accompanied by excavation of 2,041 shovel tests.
Shovel tests were approximately 30 cm in diameter and were dug to either the clay horizon or to
80 cm below the surface. Density of shovel tests was contractually a minimum of 0.3 tests per
acre, but empirically ranged from a minimum of 0.6 tests per acre at the Sunset Ridge parcel at
Lake Sam Rayburn to 4.2 tests per acre at White Oak Creek Mitigation Area. Overall testing
density was 1.1 tests per acre; this is approximately equivalent to one test every 60 by 60 m grid
square.
The inventory investigated 13 archeological sites (Table 5-1). No historic buildings or structures
were present (with the exception of the collapsed cattle dipping trough on 41AG184). Five of
these archeological sites were previously documented and the inventory verified the presence of
three of these sites. The remaining two previously known sites could not be found despite shovel
testing in the areas of record. The inventory also recorded eight new archeological sites. One of
these was a historic farmstead location that had not been previously recorded.

Six tests contained isolated artifacts that were not clearly associated with any site. The remaining
1,966 tests were all negative, including 196 tests that were excavated on sites and 1,770 tests that
were dug on transects. For the inventory as a whole, one test was positive for every 27 that were
excavated.
Six of the 11 sites yielded temporally sensitive artifacts. Ceramics were recovered from six sites
and historic material was recovered from a seventh. Diagnostic projectile points were recovered
from one of the ceramic sites. No features were discovered on any of the prehistoric sites.
Although four sites were situated on small mound landforms, three of these are probably of
natural origin and only a single site (41BW76) contained an apparent archeological mound
construction.

5.2 MANAGEMENT RECOMMENDATIONS
The eligibility of any given archeological site for inclusion to the NRHP is determined by
evaluating the site’s “significance,” or its potential to contribute meaningfully to future scientific
research. Research potential is assessed by comparing the types of data that are known - or are
suspected - to exist at the site, together with their provenience, context, and integrity, against a
set of research questions that have been previously recognized for similar sites in the region.
Of the 13 sites that are located within the inventoried areas, five sites are recommended as not
eligible for inclusion to the NRHP and one site will not be affected by the proposed undertaking.
The eligibility of the remaining eight sites is undetermined.
A summary of site
recommendations is presented in Table 5-3.

5.2.1 Sites Not NRHP Eligible
Research potential is assessed as very low to negligible for five sites: 41AG183, 41AG184,
41BW252, 41BW691, and 41JP151. These sites are evaluated as not eligible for inclusion to the
NRHP and no further management is recommended for these sites.
•

Site 41AG183 is newly discovered, ceramic period site. It appears to be a single component
site but has artifacts that have been excessively dispersed through the soil profile. It is likely
that this site has poor spatial integrity and its research potential is assessed as low.

Ecological Communications Corporation

Page 55

Cultural Resource Inventories of Selected Areas at Four Lakes in East Texas

•

Site 41AG184 is a newly recorded historic farmstead site. Artifacts found on the site suggest
it dates to the mid 19th to early 20th centuries. Sparse artifacts were found scattered over an
area 400 m in diameter. No buildings or structures are present, other than two concrete
features. Neither feature retains any structural integrity. As a result, the potential for
valuable research at this site is assessed as low.

•

Site 41JP151 is a newly discovered prehistoric aceramic site. The site is shallow and may
retain some integrity, but is small and has a low density and low diversity of artifacts. As a
result, the potential for valuable research at this site is assessed as low.

•

Site 41BW691 is a newly discovered prehistoric aceramic site. The site is shallow and may
retain some integrity, but is small and has a low density and low diversity of artifacts. As a
result, the potential for valuable research at this site is assessed as low.

•

Site 41BW252 is a previously reported ceramic period site. The site has been destroyed by
road construction activities and has no remaining research potential.

5.2.2 Sites Not Affected
One previously reported site is located very near the APE but there is no evidence for this site
within the APE and the proposed undertaking will not affect it.
•

Site 41MR108 is plotted immediately south of sub-parcel C at Ferrell’s Dam but the site does
not extend within the proposed APE and it will not be affected by the proposed undertaking.

5.2.3 Sites with Undetermined NRHP Eligibility
The shovel testing program suggests that two sites have excellent potential for further research.
Should formal site testing be conducted, it will very likely determine that these sites are eligible
for inclusion to the NRHP. Both sites should be treated as if they were eligible and should be
protected from adverse impacts.
•

41BW76 is a previously recorded prehistoric site with demonstrated high density and
diversity of artifacts. The site is situated on a mound feature which may suggest a village site.
The assemblage includes lithics, ceramics, bone, and shell and suggests possible research
into several domains including chronology; subsistence; trade and interaction; and site
structure and patterning. The site is about four acres in area and is fairly well defined.
Finally, the restricted vertical distribution of artifacts suggests deposits in good context.

•

Site 41JP152 is a previously recorded prehistoric site with high density and diversity of
artifacts. These include lithics, ceramics, bone, and shell. Research is suggested into several
domains including chronology; subsistence; trade and interaction; and site structure and
patterning. The site measures about two acres in size and is fairly well defined. In addition,
the restricted vertical distribution of artifacts suggests deposits in good context.

Page 56

Ecological Communications Corporation

Cultural Resource Inventories of Selected Areas at Four Lakes in East Texas

A clear assessment of research potential could not be achieved for five sites. Using the limited
shovel testing inventory tactics, a clear site evaluation could not be reached and it is unknown
whether or not these sites may be eligible for inclusion to the NRHP. These sites should be
protected from adverse impacts. If they can con be protected, they should be further investigated
to clearly determine NRHP eligibility.
•

Site 41BW690 is a newly discovered prehistoric aceramic site with moderate to good spatial
integrity and with promising artifact density. It is situated on a low mound which may
suggest a habitation site and/or the presence of subsurface features. However, important
questions remain unanswered about the diversity and integrity of archeological data sets on
this site and more subsurface archeological information is required to clearly assess research
potential.

•

Site 41AG182 is a newly discovered prehistoric ceramic period site with moderate to good
spatial integrity and with promising artifact density. Important questions remain unanswered
about the diversity and integrity of archeological data sets on this site and more subsurface
archeological information is needed to clearly assess research potential.

•

Site 41JP153 is a newly discovered prehistoric ceramic period site with moderate to good
spatial integrity and with promising artifact density. It is situated on a low mound which
may suggest a habitation site and/or the presence of subsurface features. However, important
questions remain about the diversity and integrity of archeological data sets on this site.
More subsurface archeological information is required to clearly assess the site’s research
potential.

•

Site 41MX29 is a previously recorded prehistoric lithic site. It consists of a small mound near
a creek but the site is without ceramics. There is some evidence that the mound may be of
recent construction and important questions remain unanswered about the integrity of
deposits. More sub-surface information is required to clearly assess research potential.

•

Site 41MX30 is a previously recorded prehistoric ceramic component site. It is situated along
the crest of a long terrace and does not extend below the landform onto the flood plain below.
Important questions remain unanswered about assemblage diversity, chronology, and the
integrity of deposits. More sub-surface archeological information is required to clearly
assess its research potential.
